## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics (classical mechanics)
**Analysis**: This task seeks the acceleration equation for a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration dv_dt is determined by restoring forces (functions of x), damping forces (functions of v), and possibly external driving (functions of t), with nonlinear terms distinguishing it from simple harmonic motion.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (nonlinear damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear damping)
- Forced Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (forced nonlinear oscillator)
- Forced damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (periodic driving)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (c1 + cos(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (quadratic nonlinearity, asymmetric potential)
- General polynomial restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (asymmetric + cubic)
- Nonlinear damping + Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * x**2 * v + c4 * v**3 (combined nonlinearities)
- Mathieu-Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x * (c1 + cos(c2 * t)) + c3 * x**3 + c4 * v (parametric + Duffing)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric potential well; even powers (x²) → asymmetric potential
- Velocity-dependent terms with position coupling (x²v) → amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-excited oscillators
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) → external periodic forcing or parametric excitation
- Product of x and trigonometric function of t → parametric resonance mechanism
- Negative linear damping combined with cubic velocity term (c₁v + c₂v³ with opposite signs) → limit cycle behavior
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system; presence → non-autonomous with possible chaos
- Rational restoring force x/(1+x²) → bounded nonlinear restoring force modeling finite-range interactions
- Sign-preserving nonlinear damping v*Abs(v) → quadratic drag that always opposes motion

GT: -beta*log(Abs(v) + c0) - c1*beta*v - omega0**c2*x**c3

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `-0.661172493025524*v - 1.16984597672115*x**3 - 0.330586246512762*log(Abs(v) + 1)`

This has three terms:
1. A term proportional to `v`
2. A term proportional to `x**3`
3. A term involving `log(|v| + 1)`

The key challenge is matching `log(|v| + 1)`. Let me note that `|v|` makes this non-analytic at v=0, which is difficult to represent with standard smooth functions.

However, let me look at candidates that contain `log` terms:

**Candidate 5:** `c0 + c1*x**3 + c2*v + c3*v**c4 + c5*log(c6*v + 1) + c7*v**2 + c8*v**c9`

This has `log(c6*v + 1)`, not `log(|v| + 1)`. The absolute value matters - `log(|v|+1)` is an even function of v (symmetric), while `log(c6*v+1)` is not. So this can't match for all v.

**Candidate 11:** Same issue with `log(c6*v + 1)`.

**Candidate 32:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*v + c3*v**c4 + c5*log(c6*v + 1) + c7*v**3 + v**2` - Same log issue, plus has fixed `v**2` term.

Now, can any combination of power terms `v**c` approximate `log(|v|+1)`? No - we need exact equivalence for all v.

Let me reconsider. The GT has `log(Abs(v) + 1)`. Could power-law terms or rational terms replicate this? No, `log` is transcendental and can't be expressed as a finite combination of powers and rationals.

Could `exp` terms help? No, `exp` and `log` aren't inverses in this context of function composition.

Wait - let me reconsider candidate 5 more carefully. The GT has `log(|v| + 1)`. If we restrict to `v ≥ 0`, then `|v| = v` and `log(|v|+1) = log(v+1)`. But the GT must hold for ALL v values, including negative ones.

Actually, let me re-examine the GT. The expression says `log(Abs(v) + c0)` with c0=1. For negative v, `|v| + 1 = -v + 1 = 1-v`, and `log(1-v)`. For positive v, it's `log(1+v)`.

So `log(|v|+1)` can be written as: for v≥0: `log(1+v)`, for v<0: `log(1-v)`.

No combination of smooth functions (polynomials, exponentials, single log) can reproduce this non-smooth behavior at v=0.

However, could power terms with non-integer exponents help? `v**c` for non-integer c is typically undefined for negative v, or involves |v|. Let me think about `c3*v**c4` - if c4 is interpreted as allowing `|v|**c4 * sign(v)` or similar... Actually in many symbolic regression frameworks, `v**c` for non-integer c might implicitly use `|v|**c` or be restricted to positive v.

But mathematically, for exact equivalence over all real v, none of these candidates can reproduce `log(|v|+1)` exactly using power laws, exponentials, rationals, or `log(cv+1)`.

**Candidate 5** with `log(c6*v + 1)`: Setting c6=1 gives `log(v+1)` which only matches for v≥0. For v<0, we'd need `log(1-v)` instead. The other terms (powers of v) can't compensate for this difference since `log(1+v) - log(1-v)` is not a polynomial/power function.

After careful analysis of all 50 candidates, none can exactly reproduce `log(|v| + 1)` for all real v. The `log` candidates use `log(cv+1)` which lacks the absolute value, and no combination of the other available terms (powers, exponentials, rationals, sin) can compensate.

Even rational functions like `v/(c+v)` or `1/(c+v)` cannot reproduce logarithmic behavior exactly.

Let me verify: Could any combination of `v**c` terms with non-integer exponents somehow produce a log? No — `v**c` for fixed `c` is a power function, not a logarithm. They are fundamentally different function classes.
